However, this is not a humidifier and it won't put enough moisture into the air to help with dry skin or allergies. Its function is to diffuse aromatic oils and for that it works just fine.<br /><br />The diffuser comes with a plastic measuring cup for the water that's marked with milliliters on both sides (no English measurements). Filling it is easy: just take the plastic cone-shaped top off, pour water from the measuring cup into the diffuser, replace the top, and turn it on. Pressing the power button once turns on the mist and the light cycling. Pressing it a second time fixes the color of the LEDs, so you can turn it on, wait until your favorite color shows up, then stop the color cycling. The colors range from turquoise to deep blue, light and dark green, and red. There's really no orange or yellow. Pressing the power button a third time turns off the LEDs but keeps the mist on. However, the power button still remains lit, and the LEDs are on at a very low setting, so the diffuser will not be totally dark. Pressing the power button a fourth time turns everything off.<br /><br />Mist comes out of the diffuser almost immediately. My advice is not to get curious and take the top off while it's running. Okay, do it once: but make sure you have a paper towel handy. I had to peek inside at the LEDs and the thing splattered water on my desk. It's not designed to run without the cone-shaped top in place and there is NO leakage when it's used as directed.   268. Just opened the box and set it up, so these are first impressions:<br /><br />PRICE: I chose the Dew after coveting the MUJI diffuser at their website, but even on sale with shipping MUJI's small diffusler came close to $120. At under $50, I'm very satisfied with the Dew.<br /><br />APPEARANCE: The photo doesn't do the Dew justice. In fact, the photo looks cheesy, but the unit itself, though lightweight, is attractively and simply designed. I put ten drops of essential oil in (the pamphlet suggests up to 5) and it's scenting my room very nicely.<br /><br />SIZE: It's about 8 inches across and about 4 inches tall. It has a nice sized footprint and is very stable. I didn't want too large a unit and this takes up as much space as if I'd stretched my fingers out and traced around the tips to form a circle.<br /><br />COLOR: The unit I bought is pure white, and no color is evident until you turn it on. The color changing feature sounds tacky, but is really quite soothing with the shift in colors almost mesmerizing. Instead of staying on a single color for very long, they blend together and change so you get dozens of shades as the unit transitions from color to color. And the agitation of the water inside the unit provides an undulating, fluttery look to the lighting; it's not a completely solid glow, it has a subtle flicker. I like the fact that you can push the button and freeze the Dew in a single color mode; with all the transitions, it gives you unlimited options to change the lighting to match your mood.<br /><br />VAPOR: It's very fine, and if you place your fingers right at the exit hole at the top, the steam comes out slightly warm, but two inches above it has no distinguishable temperature. The vapor is very fine and dissipates quickly -- it reminds me of those old &#34;genie in a bottle&#34; stories. This doesn't really humidify, which I didn't want -- I just wanted the aromatherapy benefits.<br /><br />SOUND: There is a very slight noise when it runs -- a very mild hum that is not at all distracting, and the movement of the water creates occasional droplet sounds. It's almost like white noise and I don't imagine it would be a problem to fall asleep to.<br /><br />I've been running it for a solid hour and the water level seems to have barely budged, so I can't say how long this will run until it runs out and shuts off, but I'm very satisfied with it and would highly recommend it. If it avoids the problems others have mentioned about not running after a while, I would say this is a fantastic buy.y mild hum that is not at all distracting, and the movement of the water creates occasional droplet sounds.   529. I will compare this ZAQ diffuser with the Essential Oil Diffuser by Deneve, since I ordered both of them and spent quite a bit of time reviewing all the different diffusers offered on Amazon. I'm very happy with both diffusers, but there are some differences. These two had the best ratio of 5-star reviews to 1-star reviews. Both the ZAQ and Deneve diffusers have the same size water compartment. I haven't timed how long they last on one fill, but since the ZAQ emits a greater volume of vapor per second, I would assume that it would last a shorter time between fills. The ZAQ is a little larger and does take up quite a bit of space on the table. The Deneve is also larger than I expected but I've gotten used to it. The ZAQ diffuser emits a louder whirring sound than the Deneve, so I wouldn't recommend it for the bedroom. And even though you turn off the light, it still puts off a noticeable blue glow, which is okay if you want a nightlight. It also emits a larger amount of vapor per second, so it's better for a larger room. But you wouldn't want to put it on nice furniture without some type of cloth beneath it because the vapor sometimes finds it's way to the table and leaves a damp ring around it. I use the Deneve in my bedroom because it doesn't leave any vapor around the base on my nice table, and when you click it to the no-light setting, it emits no light at all. It does put out a smaller stream of vapor, but in a smaller room it's okay. And it emits only a very light gurgling sound, which I find soothing. I've had both diffusers for about two weeks and both are working perfectly.
